  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

This character deserved better than that she was the hot nerd who laughed at the popular girls but had such a sad lifel!!!!!!</a>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Both Leah and Olivia had sad lives, the beauty in all of it was Olivia's strength to overcome and keep trying and prevailing. Leah was weak and self c<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Both Leah and Olivia had sad lives, the beauty in all of it was Olivia's strength to overcome and keep trying and prevailing. Leah was weak and self centered and didn't do anything to prevail or become a better person. People who don't own their mistakes never learn and always suffer and that is Leah.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div id="review_466952569" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466952569" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13247178-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473718933p2/13247178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466952569?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/13247178-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13247178-debra?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466952569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15960823267637447293"><br/><b>Sooooo....</b><br/><p>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/438283.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</p> <b><i>This</i> is how it feels like to be inside the mind of a child-hating, friends-judging, men-stealing manipulative woman with <u>no boundaries</u> whatsoever to get exactly what she wants when she wants it.</b><br/><br/><br/>I have to admit, I was a little apprehensive about starting this book. <i>The Opportunist</i> was easily one of the best books I've read this year (or any other year for that matter) and it made me become a huge fan of Tarryn Fisher as an author. So, why would I have second thoughts about starting</span>
  <span id="freeText15960823267637447293" style="display:none"><br><b>Sooooo....</b><br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/438283.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p> <b><i>This</i> is how it feels like to be inside the mind of a child-hating, friends-judging, men-stealing manipulative woman with <u>no boundaries</u> whatsoever to get exactly what she wants when she wants it.</b><br><br><br>I have to admit, I was a little apprehensive about starting this book. <i>The Opportunist</i> was easily one of the best books I've read this year (or any other year for that matter) and it made me become a huge fan of Tarryn Fisher as an author. So, why would I have second thoughts about starting the sequel to one of my all time favorite books you might ask? Well, because this time the sequel was written in the point of view of a characters I truly despise...<br><br><br><b>
  <i><u>Warning:</u> this review contains <u>spoilers</u> for those who haven't read the first part of the series...</i>
</b><br><br><br>Meet <b>Leah Smith--</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399280i/772471.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"My name is Leah and I will do anything to keep my husband."</i>
</b><br><br>While the first part of the Love Me With Lies - series was the story of Olivia, the Opportunist, <b>Dirty Red</b> is the story of Leah (aka Red). She's a wife, a mother, a friend, a sister and she pretty much sucks at being either of those. What she cares more than anything about is to keep hur husband, Caleb, for herself and for that she is willing to do <i>anything</i>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I have done a number of things to keep this man. I have lied and cheated. I have been sexy and meek, fierce and vulnerable. I have been everything but myself."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>It wasn't always easy to try and understand why Leah did things the way she did, but because of the way the author described it, I was able to put my feelings aside and after a while I became captivated by the story despite my original hatred towards the main character. <br><br>The story also introduces a new character, Sam, the "manny". His honesty and straightforwardness were really refreshing and I liked that he wasn't afraid to speak his mind to Leah.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Shit, I forgot," he says. "It's hard to remember that a cold shrew like you is actually a mother."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>What's better is that Leah actually seemed to accept the fact that he was so honest. They scenes between them were some of my favorites and it was interesting to watch how their "friendship" evolved.<br><br>The story alternated between the present and the past and most of Leah's inner monologues consisted of her recalling all the events that happened in <i>The Opportunist</i>. Some of the her inner monologues really showed her selfish and immature side that made me think...<p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399280ra/772472.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p>Seriously, grow up!!! I will not go into detail, but some of the things she did as a new mom were truly awful <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Who drops their newborn at a daycare for so many hours and then forgets to pick them up!?!? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br> <br><br>This book also taught me that Caleb isn't at all as perfect as he always seemed to be. He isn't the poor victim. He knew what he was doing all along and he took advantage of both Leah and Olivia's unconditional love, especially of Leah's, to get what he wanted. It made me finally see him as the strategist he really is. What I did like about him, was that finally began seeing Leah for what she really is and that he stood up for his daughter the way he did.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You said you would never hurt me." His eyes are frigid. "That was before you fucked with my daughter."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>What disappointed me a little while reading <i>Dirty Red</i> was that Olivia barely made an appearance in it. She was only in a small amount of scenes. But then off course whenever she did make an appearance, she always reminded me again of how much I loved her character by putting Leah in her place with some effective or snarky comment... <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>~ "I thought you loved your husband."<br>~ "I love yours too."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399280i/772473.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As Olivia's best friend Cammie (who was even more in the book than Olivia herself(!) but who's character I absolutely LOVED) pointed out so eloquently while she was talking about Caleb and Olivia...<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"They spark. When they're together, it's like putting a hurricane and a tornado in the same room - you can feel the tension. I didn't believe in the cliché of soul mates until I saw them together.<br>It's only a matter of time before the Caleb/Olivia saga starts up again..."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Hopefully their saga will continue in the next book Thief! I have to admit, all I want is for them to finally be together <i>without</i> either of them playing games or making up lies to get what they want. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I know, Olivia is happy now with sexy Ghandi and all <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but still, when both her and Caleb finally come clean and drop all their boundaries I think they would have a real shot at being happy. That is off course, as long as Leah doesn't come between them again... <br><br>By the end of the story I was somehow starting to feel sorry for Leah, after all she did give up everything she had to try and keep a man to who she <i>knew</i> she would always be a second choice. And I was actually starting to not <i>hate</i> her anymore. But <i>then</i>, off course, she had to go ahead and drop another bomb, that made me go...<br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/396905.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Some people never change, I guess I'm one of them." ~ Leah</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/540377.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed reading the second part of this enticing series. It provided us with some very interesting insights on how Caleb and Leah's relationship developed but other than that the book didn't teach us a lot of new things, it was mostly about Leah's feelings. I think the author really deserves credit for deciding to write a book based on such an easy-to-hate character and then still making readers able to love reading it so much! Although, after this book, I feel like I've been inside Leah's mind more than enough and now I can't wait for Caleb's POV in the third part of the series, Thief!!!<br><br><br>****</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15960823267637447293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_483236285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483236285" />
    <a title="Tough Critic Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5336035-tough-critic-book-reviews"><img alt="Tough Critic Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345668583p2/5336035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/483236285?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tough Critic Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tough Critic Book Reviews" href="/user/show/5336035-tough-critic-book-reviews">Tough Critic Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483236285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14795977152665009741"><b>Now that I've been thoroughly mind f--ked, I need a cigarette...</b><br/><br/>I'm going to let y'all in on a little secret. Ready?...I was 100% prepared not to like <i>Dirty Red</i>. I was really hoping that I would, but who really gives a damn about Leah? I sure as hell don't. Since when does the resident bitch get her own book? <br/><br/>I wanted to stomp my foot like a petulant child, throw something that would make a nice shatter noise and yell..."Why do I have to read a book about f--king Leah?" (except I'm a child so I </span>
  <span id="freeText14795977152665009741" style="display:none"><b>Now that I've been thoroughly mind f--ked, I need a cigarette...</b><br /><br />I'm going to let y'all in on a little secret. Ready?...I was 100% prepared not to like <i>Dirty Red</i>. I was really hoping that I would, but who really gives a damn about Leah? I sure as hell don't. Since when does the resident bitch get her own book? <br /><br />I wanted to stomp my foot like a petulant child, throw something that would make a nice shatter noise and yell..."Why do I have to read a book about f--king Leah?" (except I'm a child so I probably wouldn't use the "f" word) I knew I'd feel like a dog in heat humping the leg of <i>Dirty Red</i>. Begging the entire time for a few Caleb and Olivia scraps; hoping Tarryn would just throw me something...anything. Why Leah!?<br /><br />Despite my not so slight reservations I decided to give the author a chance to prove me wrong. If anyone could manipulate me to enjoy something I hate...it's Tarryn Fisher. If anyone could get inside my head and change my very emotions to work with the story instead of against it...it's Tarryn Fisher. If anyone could gift me something I didn't even know I wanted...it's Tarryn Fisher. <i>This</i> is what I wanted. I just didn't know it yet.<br /><br />Where <i>The Opportunist</i> was more about angst and emotional bipolarism, <i>Dirty Red</i> was about manipulation and it felt amazing. I read this book straight through without stopping, without for one second being detached, uninterested, or without feeling. I was fully...<i>fully</i> invested in a story about someone I cared nothing about. Manipulation!!<br /><br />One of my favorite things about Tarryn Fisher is the vagueness of her writing. We don't get every conversation or tiresome detail. She gives just enough for the development of an emotionally charged and controversial plot, but at the same time allows the reader to develop their own details, draw their own conclusions. We are given the freedom, in our minds, to create our own version of <i>Dirty Red</i><br /><br />I didn't expect...I didn't expect <i>that</i>. I didn't expect to find so much humor in <i>Dirty Red</i>. I didn't expect to fall so much more in love with Caleb. I didn't expect to find answers to so many questions only to create new ones. I didn't expect to love this book so damn much. <br /><br />Tarryn Fisher once again proves that a book isn't about loving it or hating it. It's about the emotional journey the book has the potential to take you on. The potential it has to make you feel. <br /><br />It's about the experience, an experience that will change the way you look at everything! I can't wait for the sequel!! READ ON!!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14795977152665009741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_624630260" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/624630260" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/624630260?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=rich-guys">rich-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=pregnant-heroines">pregnant-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer624630260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13573392347168207423">Love, love, love this series! <br/><br/>After getting Olivia's side of the story in 'The Opportunist', it was a change of pace to follow it with Leah's side of the story. I absolutely hated Leah in the first book, even if I sympathized with her situation. So, I wasn't sure whether or not I would be able to enjoy the story from her perspective.<br/><br/>Oddly enough, I did enjoy it immensely, but I'm having a hard time explaining why I did. This is perhaps the first time that I've read a story where I despised the m</span>
  <span id="freeText13573392347168207423" style="display:none">Love, love, love this series! <br /><br />After getting Olivia's side of the story in 'The Opportunist', it was a change of pace to follow it with Leah's side of the story. I absolutely hated Leah in the first book, even if I sympathized with her situation. So, I wasn't sure whether or not I would be able to enjoy the story from her perspective.<br /><br />Oddly enough, I did enjoy it immensely, but I'm having a hard time explaining why I did. This is perhaps the first time that I've read a story where I despised the main character from start to finish. Not only did Leah fail to redeem herself, but she became even more despicable as the book progressed. This was truly one wicked woman! I rooted against her the entire time. Yet, I loved every minute of this screwed up story. How bizarre is that?<br /><br />In some ways, I did come to see Leah as a flawed human. I felt bad for her for having such a terrible upbringing. I also pitied her for her undying devotion to Caleb. It was just sad to see the lengths she was willing to go to for a man that was clearly in love with another woman.<br /><br />However, every time I began to feel too much for Leah, another one of her conniving actions would be revealed. I could not believe some of the manipulative stunts that she pulled. Olivia has nothing on this lady in the crazy department. <br /><br />Nonetheless, I couldn't pull myself away from this story. I loved every sordid detail. This twisted love triangle has become my new obsession. On to book 3!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13573392347168207423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_673411491" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/673411491" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/673411491?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer673411491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15248649599271526493"><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430006i/861876._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> HOLY HELL. What an absolutely BRILLIANT book. 5+ stars!! </b><br/><br/>** FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED BELOW **<br/><br/>This is a book about a <b> <i> villain </i> </b>. I was morbidly curious about it and yet very apprehensive. I couldn't imagine enjoying a book that was told entirely from the perspective of a selfish, manipulative liar. I was sure I would hate it and, in truth I don't think I have <em>ever</em> hated a character as much as I did Leah but I absolutely <em>
  <strong>loved</strong>
</em> the book and that is a true testament to the strength and pure geni</span>
  <span id="freeText15248649599271526493" style="display:none"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430006i/861876._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> HOLY HELL. What an absolutely BRILLIANT book. 5+ stars!! </b><br><br>** FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED BELOW **<br><br>This is a book about a <b> <i> villain </i> </b>. I was morbidly curious about it and yet very apprehensive. I couldn't imagine enjoying a book that was told entirely from the perspective of a selfish, manipulative liar. I was sure I would hate it and, in truth I don't think I have <em>ever</em> hated a character as much as I did Leah but I absolutely <em>
  <strong>loved</strong>
</em> the book and that is a true testament to the strength and pure genius of Tarryn Fisher's writing.<br><br>That being said, Leah was just a a vile, venomous snake. She was the master of power play and manipulation and this book delves right into the twisted mind of a selfish, self-absorbed, cold-hearted, conniving, jealousy-plagued woman willing to go to any lengths to keep her prize. Any. Lengths.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"I have done a number of things to keep this man. I have lied and cheated. I have been sexy and meek, fierce and vulnerable. I have been everything but myself. He is mine right now, but I am never enough for him. I can feel it - see it in the way he looks at me. His eyes are always probing, searching for something. I don't know what he's looking for. I wish I did…</strong>
  </em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>
    <strong> I am who I am.</strong>
  </em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>
    <strong>My name is Leah, and I will do anything to keep my husband."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"I want what Olivia has. I want to be enough for him... I'll never leave him. If I leave him, she wins."</em>
</blockquote><br>The first line of this book gutted me. Totally gutted me. H.o.l.y.   H.e.l.l.<br><br>I was in shock - absolute <em>shock</em> - and after reading the first two pages, I'd decided without a shadow of a doubt that I would hate Leah forever for that. It was as though she'd been born without a moral compass.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"I picture myself hogtying Olivia and dumping her in the Everglades for the gators to deal with. Of course I would never do that - I would hire someone to do it for me."</em>
</blockquote><br>I'm not going to say anything about the plot because honestly, anything I say will be a spoiler for book #1 and I don't to ruin the experience for anyone because reading this series truly is an journey worth taking.<br><br>Suffice it to say that this is Leah's story and is told entirely from her POV. It is a direct continuation timeline-wise from where book #1 left off but has many flashbacks scattered throughout that help fill in blanks from the past and further tie the pieces of this brilliantly tangled mess of a story together.<br><br>Because of the way the story gets you right into her mind though, I could see that at her core she was really just a very damaged, insecure woman woman. But then again, everyone has damage of some kind and there is a point where being damaged can no longer suffice as an excuse. Her insecurities took her into the land of psycho. I could understand where she was coming from because her backstory gave us insight into <em>why</em> she was insecure and I mean her husband was in love with another woman and she knew it from the first time they'd met so her feelings were understandable to a certain extent but her actions were not. It went too far. Especially the way she handled the new development in this story line (spoiler which I can't talk about) - honest to goodness, that just made me sick to my stomach.<br><br>The writing is just pure brilliance! The descriptions, the details, the emotions, the dialogue, the subtext, the layers upon layers upon layers were woven together in such a way that despite how much I hated Leah, I enjoyed every word of this book.<br><br>This was the first time I'd read a book about a character like her and admittedly, it <em>was</em> fascinating to see her thoughts, learn what spurned all of her hateful actions, watch her twist reality over and over again to continually paint herself as the victim.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>“No! I think. I am not the poisonous snake. Olivia is. Everything that I’ve had to do is her fault. I am innocent.”</em>
</blockquote><br>I read the entire book with this angsty, almost queesy feeling in my heart. I was lightheaded. At times I felt like I wanted to throw up. It was worse than anything I'd felt in book one. <br><br><b> It was like watching your favorite puppy walk right into a nest of vipers. </b><br><br>There were moments in the book where I wanted to be able to feel bad for her. But then she'd do something just so horrid that it would wash away my pity and replace it with seething hatred. I waffled back and forth between hatred and pity but mostly ended up sitting on the hatred side of the fence.<br><br>Maybe if she hadn't so thoroughly fucked up the lives of the characters I cared about, I might have been able to  but... I just HATED her. She disgusted me. She was a pathetic wretch of a person who was just too selfish and manipulative for me to ever be able to truly pity.<br><br>We don't see much of Olivia in this book but her brief appearances are just epic and every hint of an appearance or reference to her gave me heart palpitations.  There is one scene though in particular where I have almost two solid pages of text highlighted because of how absolutely phenomenal it was.<br><br>I'm really looking forward to reading Caleb's POV next because I want to see what on earth he was thinking with Leah. How could he not see how soulless she was? There are so questions to which I desperately need answers.<br><br>A relationship like the once Caleb and Leah had simply wasn't built to last. When the entire framework is build on a foundation of broken hearts and lies, it's inevitable that it will all come crumbling down... it was just a matter of <em>when.</em><br><br>Caleb and Olivia were and always had been meant for each other. They knew it. I knew it. Leah even knew it.... it was just a question of the right people figuring that out and hoping that once they did, it wouldn't be too late to salvage this once in a lifetime love.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"They spark… when they're together, it's like putting a hurricane and a tornado in the same room - you can feel the tension. I didn't believe in the cliche of soul mates until I saw them together."</em>
</blockquote><br>It is so rare for me to love a book  with a love triangle in it. But the reason I loved this one as much as I did was the same reason I loved <i> Thoughtless </i>: I never, for one single moment, doubted Caleb and Olivia's love for each other. There was no 'question' as to who should end up with who.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>“I didn’t choose her,” his voice breaks. “Love is illogical. You fall into it like a manhole. Then you’re just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love.”</em>
</blockquote><br>There were some seriously EPIC lines in this book. Epic. Epic. <strong>
  <em>Epic</em>
</strong>.!!!!! The ending just built and built and the layer of the story wove themselves into place. More lies were uncovered and finally many truths came out into the light and we were left with a revelation that left me dumfounded with my jaw on the floor. Utterly in <em>shock!!</em><br><br>Tarryn Fisher is masterfully gifted with words. Without a doubt, this is one of the best written series I've read. From the first word to the last, I felt fully connected to every single word of this story.<br><br>I'm going straight on to the final book. This series has taken over my life and my heart. I can't function until I see how it all ends.<br><br>If you haven't yet taken the plunge and started these, do it now!!!!!! They are an absolutely unforgettable roller coaster. I can't recommend them highly enough!!!<br><br>5+ stars!!<br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380429893i/861591._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404021i/786137._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380429835i/861407._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> For more of my reviews, visit <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aestas Book Blog</a><br><br>And come join the Aestas Book Blog <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook Page</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15248649599271526493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393905063?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexis *Reality Bites*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexis *Reality Bites*" href="/user/show/5587514-alexis-reality-bites">Alexis *Reality Bites*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393905063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3145033596061058140">THIS REVIEW CONTAINS MINOR SPOILERS<br/>3.5 close to 4 STARS out of 5<br/>Genre: Adult Fiction<br/><b>Warning:</b> Do not read if you have not read book one in this series.<br/><i>
  <b><br/>'One thing to know about me: I dig. If I can’t find it — I dig deeper, harder. I dig until I find it. The only thing I couldn’t dig into was my own mind. I didn’t want to see it.'</b>
</i> ~ Inner monologue of Leah<br/><br/><a href='http://s1308.photobucket.com/albums/s607/aim4fashion/?action=view&current=redheads-500-41.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380387993i/748322.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>My first clear thought is that I want to make him pay. I flash to an irrational thought, where I picture myself hogtying Olivia and du</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText3145033596061058140" style="display:none">THIS REVIEW CONTAINS MINOR SPOILERS<br>3.5 close to 4 STARS out of 5<br>Genre: Adult Fiction<br><b>Warning:</b> Do not read if you have not read book one in this series.<br><i>
  <b><br>'One thing to know about me: I dig. If I can’t find it — I dig deeper, harder. I dig until I find it. The only thing I couldn’t dig into was my own mind. I didn’t want to see it.'</b>
</i> ~ Inner monologue of Leah<br><br><a href="http://s1308.photobucket.com/albums/s607/aim4fashion/?action=view&amp;current=redheads-500-41.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380387993i/748322.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>My first clear thought is that I want to make him pay. I flash to an irrational thought, where I picture myself hogtying Olivia and dumping her in the Everglades for the gators to deal with. Of course I would never do that — I would hire someone to do it for me.<br>I file through all of the other emotional bombs I can drop on him. I have told so many lies that I have an entire buffet of shadiness to choose from. I pluck out the worst one and rub my chin on my shoulder. This one will hurt him, probably deeper than anything that I could do or say about Olivia. Ready … set …</i>
</b> ~ Inner monologue of Leah<br><br><br>I...<br><br><a href="http://s1308.photobucket.com/albums/s607/aim4fashion/?action=view&amp;current=excited1.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380387993ra/748323.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Cannot even get my words out... <br><b>
  <i><br>This book was filled with lies, lies, secrets and more lies all for the sake of love...</i>
</b><br>Everything I thought about Leah going in to this book was proven wrong. In book one I enjoyed her villainous ways. However in this book I found it obsessive and obnoxious. Originally I thought I would feel some sort of pity. I thought I would start to connect with her emotionally... But no. None of that happened. Instead I hate Leah with a passion. Her heart is colder then f#cking Antarctica. And that is putting it mildly. I think the frozen tundra is more her temperature. *snaps fingers* Yes, that's it. The frozen tundra describes her best.<b> Cold. Lonely. Void of humanity.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1308.photobucket.com/albums/s607/aim4fashion/?action=view&amp;current=Frozen-Tundra-3.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380387993i/748324._SX540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br><i>
  <b>He has power over me.'</b>
</i> ~Leah<br><br><i>So much it's ridiculous</i><br>I hold nothing but hate and contempt for Leah. If I'm being honest I could consider it more of a love hate thing... I do love a good villain. But, that girl is poison. I swear that is the best way to describe her evil manipulative lying ass. She is obsessed with Caleb and on top of that she is obsessed with his obsession of Olivia. <br>Yeah, I know, the b!tch is C R A Z Y.<br><br><a href="http://s1308.photobucket.com/albums/s607/aim4fashion/?action=view&amp;current=Bitchmoment.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380387993ra/748325.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15832316.Dirty_Red__Love_Me_With_Lies___2_" title="Dirty Red (Love Me With Lies, #2) by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">Dirty Red</a> Leah follows through on her plans at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13312527.The_Opportunist__Love_Me_With_Lies___1_" title="The Opportunist (Love Me With Lies, #1) by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">The Opportunist</a>. She get's pregnant and has a baby girl named Estella Yup a girl, much to her dismay of course. Why? Because Leah is so full of herself and extremely insecure that she does not want Caleb to share his love with any other female. Leah is detached from her daughter she has no feelings what so ever for Estella. And Caleb does not take it lightly.<br><br>When Leah screws up and makes a HUGE mistake regarding Estella. Caleb decides to hire a nanny. Sam the "manny"(man-nanny) is not one to mince words. He easily takes notice to Leah's failing marriage. When Caleb is pushed to far he tells Leah they need time apart. And when she asks Sam for his advice he gives it to her straight.<br><i>
  <b><br>“How do I get him to come home?”</b>
</i> ~Leah <br><i>
  <b><br>“Get a new personality and learn to shut the fuck up.”</b>
</i> ~Sam<br><br>LOL!! Needless to say Sam provided good laughs I enjoyed him he definitely added flavor.<br><br>In the midst of all the marital woes we get flashbacks that provide some insight on Leah. <br>- How she was raised<br>- Her relationship with her parents<br>- Her interaction with other kids growing up<br>- How she copes with rejection<br> All the new information does is help confirm her status as the ice queen of the frozen tundra. Even as a kid Leah would revel in other kids misery caused by her. It was sickening. Pure and simple there is no other way to describe it.<br><br><u>Fave Lines</u><br><br><i>
  <b>“What is Dirty Red doing here?”</b>
</i> ~Cammie<br><br><i>
  <b><br>“What else are you not telling me?” <br>“Probably the same amount of stuff you’re not telling me.”</b>
</i> <br>~Leah and Caleb<br><br><i>
  <b>“You don’t own me,”</b>
</i> I say casually, but my hand is shaking as I lift my lighter. It is such a lie. Caleb has owned every one of my thoughts and actions for the last five years. ~Leah<br><br><i>
  <b>"I thought you loved your husband.”</b>
</i> She blows air through her nose. The action reminds me of an agitated horse. Her eyes rove from my shoes and land in disgust on my face. <br><i>
  <b>“I love yours too.”</b>
</i> ~Leah and Olivia<br><br><u>Fave lines unsaid</u><br><i>
  <b><br>'I am so jealous of his hurt that I throw my head back and open my mouth to scream in rage. He won’t hear me. No matter how loudly I scream his name, he will not hear me. He only hears her.'</b>
</i> ~Leah<br><i>
  <b><br>'My voice lacks conviction. I used to be such an accomplished liar.'</b>
</i><br>~Leah<br><br><u>My Thoughts</u><br><b> I must say Tarryn Fisher definitely has a way with words. They rip you and don't let go.</b> I am conflicted on how to rate it. I decided it was more of a three star book because unlike it's predecessor I was able to predict the outcome of six different plot twist. I also did not get enough Olivia I missed her and found myself craving more of her. Then there is the whole Seth thing. His character came out of nowhere. I mean.. yes, I knew Caleb was not an only child but Seth's character was out of left field. I think I would have took to him better if he was introduced to us in book 1.<br><br>Dear readers,<br>I gave this book 3.5 stars because I simply knew what was coming next with various plot-lines. I think I would have ranked it higher if we got more Olivia. I was dying to know her pov and to see her interact more with both Noah and Caleb.<b> On Goodreads rating system I allow the full four stars; because Tarry Fisher can take words and make you feel them in the full measure of which a characters says or thinks them.</b> I find that very important when reading a book. And while I did not hold empathy for Leah I was still submersed in her world wanting to know how it would all play out.<br><br> <br><br>My Ratings<br>Characters- love some hate some<br>Writing Style- Good, Tarryn Fisher has a way with words<br>Plot/Storyline- A little predictable<br>Steam Factor- Low<br>Overall- I liked it! I just desired more Olivia.<br><b><br>Now go forth and read. Then come tell us about it on Goodreads!</b><br><br>For more reviews go to <br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://realitybites-letsgetlost.blogspot.com">http://realitybites-letsgetlost.blogs...</a> <br><br><br><br><br> <br><br><br><br></span>

<div id="review_422395039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422395039" />
    <a title="Merita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2708699-merita"><img alt="Merita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353581222p2/2708699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422395039?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merita" href="/user/show/2708699-merita">Merita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422395039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3881423157421249733">7th January 2013:<br/><br/>Firstly I have to say <b> I LOVE YOU TARRYN FISHER </b> Amazing, just simply amazing. The twists, the turns, the bitchiness, the crazyness AAARRGGHHHH I loved every minute of it!!! <br/><br/>The Opportunist left us on a cliffhanger and Dirty Red filled us in on all the gaps of what we wanted to know.<br/>I have to say (and dont all kill me now) but i felt sorry for Leah, she really had a hard time growing up. In Dirty Red you get to understand Leah a little more because the book is from her point of </span>
  <span id="freeText3881423157421249733" style="display:none">7th January 2013:<br><br>Firstly I have to say <b> I LOVE YOU TARRYN FISHER </b> Amazing, just simply amazing. The twists, the turns, the bitchiness, the crazyness AAARRGGHHHH I loved every minute of it!!! <br><br>The Opportunist left us on a cliffhanger and Dirty Red filled us in on all the gaps of what we wanted to know.<br>I have to say (and dont all kill me now) but i felt sorry for Leah, she really had a hard time growing up. In Dirty Red you get to understand Leah a little more because the book is from her point of view.<br><br><b> <i> I knew he never loved me like he loved her, but I wanted him anyway. I knew his love for me was conditional, but I wanted him anyway. I knew I was second choice, but I wanted him anyway </i></b> <br><br>In The Opportunist, i hated Leah with a passion and i mean PASSION. But in Dirty Red, i got to understand her a lot more. Up until the end, then all my softness towards her changed into me thinking, she is a bitch, a real stupid bitch!! Aarrghh<br><br><br><br>At the end at 2am i was left like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392453ra/755505.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>September 26th 2012:<br><b> Sheeet i need this now!!!! </b><br><br>While googling EVERYTHING Tarryn Fisher (yes i'm a little obsessed), i came across this at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thepressedpenny.com">www.thepressedpenny.com</a><br><br><br>Dirty Red Exclusive!<br>by Nena » Mon Jun 18, 2012 5:54 am<br><br>Tarryn Fisher promised a Dirty Red spoiler to all those that have reviewed The Opportunist at amazon and she kindly offered the exclusive to The Pressed Penny as well as we are getting ready to launch the site this week. If you haven't had a chance to leave her a review make sure you do so, here is a link to the amazon page.<br><br>Also make sure to register to the forums so you can participate and take advantage of this and other exclusives in the future!<br><br>WARNING! SPOILER...<br><br>Spoiler: <br>Dirty Red<br><br>She looks the same. Raven hair hanging wildly to her waist. She is shorter than I am, but not by much. She is wearing teal, linen pants and a cream sheath shirt that hangs casually off one defined shoulder. I eye her gold hoop earrings which are big enough to fit my entire hand through. They make her look exotic and slightly dangerous. She has always made me feel plain.<br><br>Her eyes rove over the handful of occupants in the diner, searching for a face she recognizes; an old man, a couple who share the same side of a booth, two servers folding silverware into napkins…me.<br><br>I see the shock overcome her features; the parting of her lips, the slight spreading of white around her irises. Suddenly, she stiffens. Her eyes chase to the four corners of the room, and I know she is looking for him. I shake my head to tell her he’s not here. I take a sip of my coffee and I wait.<br><br>She moves with purpose toward my table, when she reaches where I am sitting, she doesn’t sit but stares at me expectantly.<br><br>“An old client?” She says dryly.<br><br>“Well, I am aren’t I?” I motion for her to sit. I’d sent an anonymous message to her office, claiming I was an old client and telling her I was in legal trouble. I’d asked her to meet me at a diner named Tiffany’s. I had no idea if she’d come or not, but it was better than showing up at her office.<br><br>She slides cautiously into the seat across from me, never taking her eyes from my face.<br><br>“Well, what the fuck do you want?”<br><br>I flinch. Louboutins or not, she’s still the same crass piece of white trash she used to be.<br><br>“I thought maybe you could look over this document for me.” I reach into my purse and pull out the papers I’d stolen from Caleb’s filing cabinet. Placing them on the table, I slide them toward her.<br>“What is this?” she asks. She eyes me distastefully, and I want to reach across the table and hack off her hair with my butter knife. How dare she look at me that way? She has single handedly ruined my life. I’d have everything if it weren’t for her devious, overreaching hands.<br>I’d probably also be in prison. I push that thought away. Now is not the time for gratitude. Now is the time for answers. I poke the document in front of her.<br><br>“Take a look. See for yourself.”<br><br>Without moving her head, she looks at the papers then back to me. It's a smooth, hard, impressive piece of intimidation. The art of her body language is something to be admired.<br><br>“Why would I want to do that?” she says.<br><br>She's making me feel chilled. I get a flashback of being on the witness stand and my heartrate spikes. I practice to see if I can do it too.<br><br>“It’s Caleb’s,” I say, only moving my lips.<br><br>I don’t know whether it’s the mention of his name or if my imitation of her body language is working, but she tenses.<br><br>A server approaches our table. Olivia reaches for papers.<br><br>“Get her a coffee, two creamers.” I say waving him away. He hurries off. Olivia, who is reading, briefly glances up at me. I spent almost every day with her for nine months. I know what she likes.<br><br>I sip my coffee as she reads, watching her face.<br><br>Her coffee arrives. Without looking up she pulls the lids from the creamers and dumps them into her cup.<br><br>She lifts the mug to her lips, but halfway there her hand freezes. Coffee spills onto the table as she slams the mug down. She stands up.<br><br>“Where did you get that?”<br><br>She is backing away from the table, shaking her head. “Why is my name on there?”<br><br>I run my tongue across my teeth. “I was hoping you could tell me that?”<br><br>She bolts for the door. I stand up, tossing a twenty on the table and go after her.<br><br>I follow her into the parking lot and corner her by the newspaper stand. “You are not getting out of explaining why your name is on this deed along with my husbands!”<br><br>Her face is washed of color. She shakes her head. “I don’t know, Leah. He never—I don’t know.”<br><br>She covers her face with her palms, and I hear her sob. That only makes me angrier. I take a threatening step toward her.<br><br>“You’re sleeping with him aren’t you?”<br><br>She pulls her hands away and glares at me.<br><br>“No. I love my husband.” She is clearly insulted that I would even accuse her of such a thing.<br>“I love mine!” My voice cracks. “-So, why does he love you?”<br>She looks at me with true loathing.<br><br>“He doesn’t,” she says simply. “He chose you.” It pains her to give me those words. I can see the bleeding emotions spilling from her skin.<br><br>I hold up the deed and shake it. “He bought you a house.”<br><br>She snatches the deed from me and points to a date. “Did you miss this little detail? —Long before you, Leah.” She shoves it back at me. “But, you know that. So, why did you really trick me into coming here?”<br><br>I swallow— a nervous reaction. She sees it and smiles cruelly.<br><br>“I should have let them throw you in prison.”<br><br>She turns away, reaching for her car door. Her statement infuriates me. I dig my fingernails into my palms and breathe through my nose.<br><br>“So you could have him?” I blurt. My blood pounds in my ears. I ask myself that question all the time. Why did she agree to defend me? Why did she win the case?<br><br>She freezes, looks at me over her shoulder.<br><br>“Yeah.”<br><br>I didn’t expect the truth. “I thought you loved your husband.”<br><br>She blows air through her nose. “I love yours too.”<br><br><br>OH MY GOD I CANT WAIT!!!!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3881423157421249733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489144410" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16681803004353629756"><a href='http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/FisherDirtyRed2TitlebySueBee_zpsa5b9c240.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402576i/782568.jpg' alt=' photo FisherDirtyRed2TitlebySueBee_zpsa5b9c240.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>★★★★ 1/2! Love Me With Lies, book 2 of 3! Leah, the villain plaguing the series gets her story!</b><br/><br/><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“I didn’t choose her,” his voice breaks. “Love is illogical. You fall into it like a manhole. Then you’re just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br/><i>
  <b>Dirty Red, book 2 in the Love Me With Lies Trilogy is written from the villain’s POV. What a brilliant idea, yet the cause of so much angst!</b>
</i><br/><br/><b>This series is really Caleb Drake’s and Olivia Kaspen’s whirlwind saga </b></span>
  <span id="freeText16681803004353629756" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/FisherDirtyRed2TitlebySueBee_zpsa5b9c240.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402576i/782568.jpg" alt=" photo FisherDirtyRed2TitlebySueBee_zpsa5b9c240.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>★★★★ 1/2! Love Me With Lies, book 2 of 3! Leah, the villain plaguing the series gets her story!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“I didn’t choose her,” his voice breaks. “Love is illogical. You fall into it like a manhole. Then you’re just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><i>
  <b>Dirty Red, book 2 in the Love Me With Lies Trilogy is written from the villain’s POV. What a brilliant idea, yet the cause of so much angst!</b>
</i><br><br><b>This series is really Caleb Drake’s and Olivia Kaspen’s whirlwind saga spanning over a decade</b> filled with love, joy, angst, anger, frustration, but mostly a <b>profound sadness for all the could-have-beens</b>. Their love, in all its dysfunction and deception, is so great it blurs the line between right and wrong, overcomes trial and tribulation with hopes of transcending time!<br><br><u>Books in Love Me With Lies series should be read in order and together:</u><br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484477044" rel="nofollow noopener">The Opportunist</a> (book 1)<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489144410" rel="nofollow noopener">Dirty Red</a> (book 2)<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489144658" rel="nofollow noopener">Thief</a> (book 3)</b><br><br><b>We first met (Johanna) Leah Smith in The Opportunist (book 1)</b>. She played a significant part in that book and will continue to do so throughout the series. In <b>Dirty Red (book 2) we get to Leah’s story</b> as it follows her from childhood to present time. It covers her <b>complicated relationship with Caleb and her dealings with Olivia. It’s a glimpse into her mind and yes there are some mitigating circumstances along with some incriminating</b>.<br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/FisherLovemewithlies1-3HeroinebySueBee_zps51a1c7ec.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380401890i/780603.jpg" alt=" photo FisherLovemewithlies1-3HeroinebySueBee_zps51a1c7ec.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There is very little of <b>Olivia Kaspen</b> in this story.<br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/FisherLovemewithlies1-3HerobySueBee_zpsfb630566.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380401890i/780604.jpg" alt=" photo FisherLovemewithlies1-3HerobySueBee_zpsfb630566.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Caleb Drake</b> continues to be an enigma. Five words to describe <b>Caleb: Captivating, enigmatic, unforgettable, conflicted and enduring</b>.<br><br><b>It was painful for me to read about the love Caleb had for Leah</b>. Though I realize it’s a reality in my book world I prefer to focus one-love-a-lifetime. The innocent Estella grabbed me and wrapped herself around my heart, but her existence was also complicating matters. I say <b>it’s time for Caleb’s POV in book 3, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489144658" rel="nofollow noopener">Thief</a></b>.<br><br><b>Ms. Fisher’s writing is exquisite and the series plot is unusual, fresh and superbly executed</b>. Yet it is difficult for me to rate this book. On one hand it is a critical part in a 5-star series, but on the other hand we are following the villain, the person standing in between Caleb and Olivia. Here is my breakdown:<br><br>***<br>Hero rating: 5 stars <br>Leah as MC: 5 stars<br>Leah as Heroine: 1 stars<br>Storyline concept rating: 4 stars<br>Storyline execution rating: 5 stars<br>Storytelling skills rating: 5 stars<br>Story ending rating: N/A<br>Book editing rating (5 = no edits spotted): 4.5 stars<br>************************************************<br><b>Overall rating: 4.5 stars<br><br>Would I recommend this series: Yes.<br>Would I re-read this series: Yes.<br>Would I read future books by this author: Yes.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIF%20heroine/QC8H4_zpsd876118d.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380402576ra/782569.gif" alt=" photo QC8H4_zpsd876118d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438059221" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11444402260043658353">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Yep, I one-starred this sucker. Here’s what I need all you fangirls to do while I explain . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://lunapic.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447173684ra/16965946.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I really dug <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1396175963?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Opportunist</a>
</i> and made the rare exception of placing Book #2 on my TBR because the storyline peaked my curiosity. I admittedly <b>HATE</b> books in a series and rarely read past the first. The reason? Because there is always SO. MUCH. FILLER. There’s hardly ever enough material to produce three (or more) books – especially in</span>
  <span id="freeText11444402260043658353" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Yep, I one-starred this sucker. Here’s what I need all you fangirls to do while I explain . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447173684ra/16965946.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I really dug <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1396175963?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Opportunist</a>
</i> and made the rare exception of placing Book #2 on my TBR because the storyline peaked my curiosity. I admittedly <b>HATE</b> books in a series and rarely read past the first. The reason? Because there is always SO. MUCH. FILLER. There’s hardly ever enough material to produce three (or more) books – especially in the romance/NA/erotica/whateveryouwanttocallthem genres. Buuuuuuuuut, when a book fairy gifts you a book in order for you to take the hit so she doesn’t have to, there’s kinda no choice but to read Book #2. Guess what I found out while reading it????<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447173299ra/16965891.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>The Opportunist</i> worked for me because #1 it was different (even with the tired trope of accident induced amnesia), #2 Olivia was an unlikable character, but you weren’t <i>supposed</i> to like her (at best she would end up as the lesser of two evils), and #3 Tarryn Fisher is bad at romance in the best way possible. I too am bad at romance, and that is why I <s>want to spend hours braiding her raven locks</s> love reading Ms. Fisher's stories. Sadly, <i>Dirty Red</i> was the book of filler and/or throw everything at the wall and see what might stick. There was the re-hashing of <i>The Opportunist’s</i> story, there were “twists” (*insert eyeroll*), there was the “character development” (I use that term in the loosest manner possible) of Big Red herself . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447173299ra/16965892.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>However, this book wasn’t <b>necessary</b> at all. Big Red was soooooo one dimensional that it became pretty clear even the author wasn’t that interested in her story. And Caleb? Nothing like getting to know someone deeper than surface level only to discover you want to smack that bitch . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447173299ra/16965893.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>All that being said, I’m still gonna read #3. (Zero shame, that is my name.) Because Tarryn Fisher has me caught up like a fish on a damn hook and I just have to find out where all this ends up . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“Love is illogical. You fall into it like a manhole. Then you’re just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love.”</i>
</b><br><br>And speaking of fish – looky looky . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447173299i/16965894._SY540_.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Introducing my newest reading buddy Billy Bass, a/k/a the only guy in my house that might be able to drink me under the table. <br><br>Many thanks to my fellow connoisseur of fine brews <a>JaHy</a> for this book hookup. Your selection ended up being the perfect excuse for imbibing <s>half a dozen</s> a couple of grown-up root beers.<br></span>

I felt that on her own Leah wasn't enough and Olivia and Caleb were barely in the book.<b>***</b><br/><br/>Dirty Red is told through the point of view of Leah Drake and sha</span>
  <span id="freeText8934900668315995956" style="display:none"><b>3-4 Ginger Stars~</b><br><br><b>THIS JUST IN...Leah Drake is found guilty of not only being a liar, a manipulator and a first class bitch, but also of being an unfit mother to poor defenseless baby Estella, so sad!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380401653i/779854.jpg" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>***The Reason for 3 - 4 Stars<br></b>I found myself for the majority of the book looking forward to her next interaction with Olivia, Caleb, Seth or Sam. I felt that on her own Leah wasn't enough and Olivia and Caleb were barely in the book.<b>***</b><br><br>Dirty Red is told through the point of view of Leah Drake and shares both past and present story lines. We learn a lot about Leah’s childhood/adolescence as well as her family dynamics. We also follow her from the moment she meets Caleb to the present.<br><br><b>
  <i>"I wondered what stupid bitch let him go. Whoever she was, I would wipe her from his memory in no time at all. Why? Because I was the best of the best: the Godiva, the Maserati, the perfect colorless diamond. I could improve anyone's life -- especially this man's."</i>
</b><br><br>As readers, we are privileged to the inner thoughts of Leah and I can tell you she really is a malicious, self-centered, manipulative, obsessive and mean redhead.<br><br>Leah gives birth to a beautiful daughter named Estella. She feels nothing for her daughter except jealousy for Caleb’s affections. When I tell you that Leah maybe of the world’s worst moms I’m not joking. Some of things she does and feels just breaks my heart.<br><br>We meet some new characters one of which I REALLY liked – Sam, the Manny!! He handles Leah perfectly throughout the story. I would love for him to be in future books. <br><br>Sometimes no matter how much you plot and plan to hold onto what you want. If it wasn’t yours to begin with you have to face the truth.<br><br><b>
  <i>"I thought you loved your husband."<br>She blows air through her nose. The action reminds of an agitated horse. Her eyes rove from my shoes and land in disgust on my face.<br>"I love yours too."</i>
</b><br><br>In a way, Dirty Red could also be called “clearing the air”. Most past deceptions on Leah and Caleb’s parts comes to light by the end of the story. <br><br><b>
  <i>"I didn't choose her," his voice breaks. "Love is illogical. You fall into it like manhole. Then you're just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love." </i>
</b>~ Caleb<br><br>Most readers will want to know if the book ends with a HEA and/or is it a cliffhanger?<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No HEA for Leah at least. We aren’t left hanging but the story isn’t over. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The last line of the story pretty much sums up Leah:<br><br><b>
  <i>”Some people never change. I guess I’m one of them.” ~ Leah Drake</i>
</b> <br><br>So I guess it ain’t over till it’s over!!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

I didn’t want to read this book. <br/><br/>I hate Leah!! I don't want to be in her mind, or hear how she feels, or go through what she goes through...I just want her to hurt badly and for the ending I WANTED (Yes I am selfish) to happen!!<br/><br/>But it is like an addiction…I had to read it. I don’t know how I feel about it because, I don’t care about Leah’s feelings or her past. I think that is Tarryn’s talent…she puts you there, she makes you l</span>
  <span id="freeText16219953575181896769" style="display:none">If you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13312527.The_Opportunist__Love_Me_with_Lies___1_" title="The Opportunist (Love Me with Lies, #1) by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">The Opportunist</a>, you probably hate Leah as much as I do. I didn’t want to read this book. <br><br>I hate Leah!! I don't want to be in her mind, or hear how she feels, or go through what she goes through...I just want her to hurt badly and for the ending I WANTED (Yes I am selfish) to happen!!<br><br>But it is like an addiction…I had to read it. I don’t know how I feel about it because, I don’t care about Leah’s feelings or her past. I think that is Tarryn’s talent…she puts you there, she makes you love Caleb, hate Leah, wish for Olivia…<br><br>You do learn about Leah’s past…her perspective…what she has done. <br><br>I hated the beginning because I kept thinking…, Great, Caleb will never leave her now!! <br><br>But he will never stop loving Olivia…<br><br><b> “You never quite stop loving someone when you’re in that deep” </b><br><br>Everyone knows it…<br><br><b> “I didn’t believe in the cliché of soul mates until I saw them together” </b><br><br><b> “It’s only a matter of time before the Caleb/Olivia saga starts up again.” </b><br><br>Even Leah knows it…<br><br><b> “I knew he never loved me like he loved her, but I wanted him anyway. I knew his love for me was conditional, but I wanted him anyway. I knew I was second choice, but I wanted him anyway. But, this was too much.” </b><br><br>Yet, everyone still keeps going through the paces. Leah does everything she can think of to keep him, Caleb is torn…and who knows what is going on with Olivia. <br><br>The ending gives me hope…I admit my jaw dropped but I have hope!!<br><br>Casting:<br><br>Leah--<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390195i/751786.jpg" width="350" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Caleb--<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390195i/751787._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Olivia--<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390195i/751788.jpg" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br> <br><br></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who are crazy and have brain problems!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6165339-akanksha-s-ren?shelf=series-continuation">series-continuation</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482834087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7637621582210402211"><b>MOTHER FUCKING HELL!!<br/>I.need.the.thrid.book.like.fucking.now.</b><br/><br/><i>There is a fucking thin line between obsession and love, and let me break it to you Leah.. Bitch you crossed that line by miles.</i><br/><br/>ITS IN FUCKING FRONT OF YOUR EYES THAT HE DOESN'T LOVE YOU, never has, never will the way he loves her.<br/><br/><b>I find it amusing how I <i>HATE</i> characters from novels I read with every fiber from my being without them even fucking being real or anything.</b><br/>How jealous and insecure can a person be?? Her level of insecurity and</span>
  <span id="freeText7637621582210402211" style="display:none"><b>MOTHER FUCKING HELL!!<br />I.need.the.thrid.book.like.fucking.now.</b><br /><br /><i>There is a fucking thin line between obsession and love, and let me break it to you Leah.. Bitch you crossed that line by miles.</i><br /><br />ITS IN FUCKING FRONT OF YOUR EYES THAT HE DOESN'T LOVE YOU, never has, never will the way he loves her.<br /><br /><b>I find it amusing how I <i>HATE</i> characters from novels I read with every fiber from my being without them even fucking being real or anything.</b><br />How jealous and insecure can a person be?? Her level of insecurity and jealousy and obsession ins't even normal, its like crazy x10<br /><br /><b>
  <i>I was about a ten on the poison scale. If he needed venom, I could inject it directly into his neck.</i>
</b><br /><br />Leah needs pills, she's like a proper crazy woman!!!! Gosh, I hate her. Proper psychopath she is!! AGRH!!! <br /><br />This book is filled with lies, secrets, backstabbing, obsession, insecurity, craziness, manipulation and plotting.<br /><br />NEVER FUCKING BE ANYONE'S SECOND CHOICE. NEVER. I'd rather fucking die alone than be replaceable.<br />And thats what you are Leah. A second choice, trash and replaceable.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I thought you loved your husband.” She blows air through her nose.<br />The action reminds me of an agitated horse. Her eyes rove from my shoes and land in disgust on my face. “I love yours too.”</i>
</b><br />Hated that there was only one scene with Olivia on this book!!! *pissed*<br />Can't wait for the third book, hope it comes ASAP!! and I am dying to know what was in that gift box! agrh<br /><br />I don't know how to even rate this book, the 5stars are ONLY for the writing, and story.. nuin for Leah!</span>

<div id="review_1165609503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165609503" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1165609503?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165609503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2725364799608136779">So, let me say that by all means, just because I gave it 3 stars doesn't mean I didn't downright love this. But, and there's a big but here, I tend to give books I have a sort of hate/love 3 stars, it's just how I work. Now I can proceed to my review.<br/><br/>Well, by the book cover and title we can all assume that this is a sequel told from Leah's perspective, and yes I never liked the girl but getting into her mind was just as dirty as the book title says. That girl, has some serious problems. She's ne</span>
  <span id="freeText2725364799608136779" style="display:none">So, let me say that by all means, just because I gave it 3 stars doesn't mean I didn't downright love this. But, and there's a big but here, I tend to give books I have a sort of hate/love 3 stars, it's just how I work. Now I can proceed to my review.<br /><br />Well, by the book cover and title we can all assume that this is a sequel told from Leah's perspective, and yes I never liked the girl but getting into her mind was just as dirty as the book title says. That girl, has some serious problems. She's needy, she can't seem to realize when it's best to walk away, and she's destroying her life all by herself. That's a common trait she shares with Olivia. <br /><br />What has made such a huge impression on me reading this series is how real it is. I mean, it shows all the real feelings that everyday people would have, but intensified or it may be that Fisher has simply made her characters really really straightforward.<br /><br />The first book had the same hold on me as this one did. Which is why I loved it so much. It was un-puttable. And while I certainly didn't like Leah anymore after finishing this, I honestly don't think that was Fisher intention. I think she wanted us to show how some people never change, and no character in this book can change themselves no matter how hard they try. <br /><br />Apart from love, there's abundant hate in this book, and mostly it's just a combination of the too. Leah sees Caleb as the prize she stole from Olivia, and that's not love, I know she thinks it is.. but no girl.<br /><br />The end of the book paved the way for book three and I honestly couldn't be more excited about it because Caleb seems to be the most fucked up character of the three, considering he's only ever done relationships with super-crazy, manipulative cheeks. I want to see what drives him to do the things he does.<br /><br />And by all means guys, read the hell out of this series. It's addictive and it'll keep you up all night reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2725364799608136779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
