<div id="review_520153515" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/520153515" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/520153515?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ♥Rachel♥ by: </span>
      Arlene 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer520153515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2448163569024036509">I was nervous picking up Dirty Red after reading The Opportunist, because frankly, I HATE LEAH!!! With the heat of a thousand suns, kind of hate. Maybe I’m being a little melodramatic, but this series brings out some pretty powerful feelings in me. Obsession is probably first and foremost. The fact that I LOVED Dirty Red as much if not more is a testament to the brilliant writing skills of Tarryn Fisher, because how else could I love a book that’s in the POV of a woman I detest? <br/><br/><b>I you haven’t re</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2448163569024036509" style="display:none">I was nervous picking up Dirty Red after reading The Opportunist, because frankly, I HATE LEAH!!! With the heat of a thousand suns, kind of hate. Maybe I’m being a little melodramatic, but this series brings out some pretty powerful feelings in me. Obsession is probably first and foremost. The fact that I LOVED Dirty Red as much if not more is a testament to the brilliant writing skills of Tarryn Fisher, because how else could I love a book that’s in the POV of a woman I detest? <br /><br /><b>I you haven’t read The Opportunist, you may want to stop reading now. It’ll spoil some things you learn in that story. </b><br /><br />We pick up the story not long after Olivia has left Caleb in Rome after her heartfelt confession. Exactly how long, is something I’m trying to figure out. It will tell me something I desperately want to know! Anyways, Olivia is now married to Noah (I think) and Leah and Caleb are married and bringing their newborn home from the hospital. If you thought Leah was bad in The Opportunist, you will cringe and die reading her thoughts on motherhood and her baby! I’m a mother and I just can’t even fathom the thoughts!! Horrible, hateful woman! Caleb however, is beyond excited at the prospect of being a father. It’s something he’s always wanted. He refuses to let Leah get a full-time nanny, and she’s horrified by the thought of taking care of this “thing” on her own, while he works. Her devious plans on getting pregnant to get and keep Caleb are about to backfire on her SPECTACULARLY, and I was glued to my kindle seeing how this all played out!<br /><br />Olivia is in the story, only peripherally and through Leah’s eyes, but she is a huge presence in Leah’s mind. Leah has always suspected that Caleb isn’t over Olivia, to the point that so many of her actions revolve around that. Oh what a tangled web we weave. Unfortunately for Leah, when you scheme and manipulate, more often than not this comes back to haunt you. <br /><br />I will say that Leah does have a sad history, but I still couldn’t excuse her intentions and actions. I really felt no pity for her at all, because people have been treated worse and not turned out like her. She had a sister who loved her, even if she came in second with her parents. If she would’ve acted more like a genuine friend to others, she would’ve had more people who cared for her. Plus, if I really felt she actually loved Caleb instead of feeling like he was her rightfully won prize, I might have been able to excuse some of her actions. That was not the case, IMO. <br /><br />Through Leah we see so much of Caleb. It gave me insight on his past with Olivia and how he feels about her now. I adore Caleb, but he was not without fault either. But Olivia and Caleb can’t stay away from each other, and it’s just a matter of time. As Cammie says: <br /><br /><b>
  <i> “When they’re together, it’s like putting a hurricane and a tornado in the same room—you can feel the tension. I didn’t believe in the cliché of soul mates until I saw them together.” <br /><br />“There is a possibility that you feel like you’re worth more than being Caleb’s marriage of pity, and if that’s true then you should jump ship now. It’s only a matter of time before the Caleb/Olivia saga starts up again.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I can’t wait!<br /><br />The last 10% of this story my jaw was on the floor with the revelations! And OH MY GOODNESS that last page, holy heck!!! Needless to say I’m on pins and needles until the third book, Thief (In Caleb’s POV!!) comes out! Caleb and Olivia have to end up together. I CAN’T imagine it any other way. At this point I’m not above camping out at Tarryn Fisher’s home to speed up the process. That’s a restraining order I’m willing to brave, lol! Just kidding. Well, sort of...<br /><br />You can read this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2013/02/review-dirty-red-by-tarryn-fisher.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2448163569024036509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2466196316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2466196316" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2466196316?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kissing-books">kissing-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2466196316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9519322754275359110"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I'm usually pretty bad about reading sequels because I'm both easily distracted and a cheapskate, so sometimes years will go by before I'll say to myself, "You know, I really liked X book, maybe it's time I should read the sequel to X book..." but of course, I never do. Or at least, I usually don't. I read the prequel to this book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2459843066' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE OPPORTUNIST</a>, just a few days ago, and I've already finished DIRTY RED with my eye on THE THIEF. It's th</span>
  <span id="freeText9519322754275359110" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I'm usually pretty bad about reading sequels because I'm both easily distracted and a cheapskate, so sometimes years will go by before I'll say to myself, "You know, I really liked X book, maybe it's time I should read the sequel to X book..." but of course, I never do. Or at least, I usually don't. I read the prequel to this book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2459843066" rel="nofollow noopener">THE OPPORTUNIST</a>, just a few days ago, and I've already finished DIRTY RED with my eye on THE THIEF. It's that addictive.<br><br><br><br>While reading, I kept wondering what this series reminded me of, and then it hit me: BIG LITTLE LIES. This <i>Love Me with Lies </i>(see? it even has "lies" in the title) is like a smuttier, trashier version of BIG LITTLE LIES. Maybe if BIG LITTLE lies were written by Jackie Collins instead of Lianne Moriarty.<br><br><br><br>The first book is written from Olivia's POV, in both "past" and "present," and we see all the scheming and conniving Olivia had to do to not just meet Caleb the first time but to steal him back later. This book is written from the "other woman", Leah's, POV, and as with Olivia, we get to see all the scheming and conniving Leah had to do to steal him again and then try to hold onto him. Not an easy task, because as we saw in THE OPPORTUNIST, Caleb's not all sweetness and light, either.<br><br><br><br>It's been a while since I read about a character who was so flawed and repulsive and yet still managed to be interesting. I think the last one was probably one of the women in that 70s potboiler classic, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2082920249" rel="nofollow noopener">VALLEY OF THE DOLLS</a>. Leah obviously has some sort of personality disorder - she's clingy, needy, manipulative, and cruel. The things she does to Caleb and then, (spoiler) to her own daughter are just awful. And yet you can't help but feel bad for her, because technically (well, not technically - <i>actually</i>) Olivia is the other woman and Leah is just trying to hold onto what's hers. The problem is that she won Caleb's affection through false pretenses, just as Olivia did, and sees him more as a prize to be won and displayed than as an actual person with thoughts and feelings. In many ways, she and Olivia are cut from the same cloth, and you find that out when more of Leah's backstory is revealed in this book and you discover just how messed up of a person she is, as well as her family.<br><br><br><br>Like THE OPPORTUNIST, this story is told in "past" and "present." The writing in this book, however, is a real step up from its prequel. The characterization is excellent, and Leah bursts from the pages in a way that Olivia really didn't - maybe because the author tried too hard to make Oliviafeel like a sympathetic character, whereas Leah just gets to completely be her wretched, awful self. I loved it. How often do you get a truly disgusting antiheroine as a protagonist? It's so rare. I devoured this book in a single day, feeling as giddy as a person working their way through a tub of illicit 2AM ice cream. I know that this is trash, but oh what decadent, glorious trash it is. I want more.<br><br><br><br><div>
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532327388ra/26015342.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</div><br><br><br>4 to 4.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="9519322754275359110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_394313641" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/394313641" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/394313641?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer394313641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11857378574673257698">Now we get Dirty Red's POV, aka Leah, the "villain" of the story. I have to admit that I was a bit apprehensive to start this book...I didn't want to end up liking Leah but thank goodness, I didn't have anything to worry about! If anything, while I may understand her a bit more...and feel a bit sadden by things that have happened to her, I still just don't like her. And she makes that very easy. <br/><br/>I enjoyed that it alternated chapters with going to the past and then coming back to what was happeni</span>
  <span id="freeText11857378574673257698" style="display:none">Now we get Dirty Red's POV, aka Leah, the "villain" of the story. I have to admit that I was a bit apprehensive to start this book...I didn't want to end up liking Leah but thank goodness, I didn't have anything to worry about! If anything, while I may understand her a bit more...and feel a bit sadden by things that have happened to her, I still just don't like her. And she makes that very easy. <br /><br />I enjoyed that it alternated chapters with going to the past and then coming back to what was happening in the present. It allowed us to get a different perspective on things that happened in the past and some answers on why they happened. And I liked seeing how things were going on now.<br /><br />I knew there would be no way that I would like this book as much as the first book, <i>The Opportunist</i>, which was amazing! I didn't want my dislike for a character to influence my feelings for the actual story. And there was no way that Leah could be redeemed, certainly not enough to be a good person. But I felt the story held its own. <br /><br />Leah was certainly interesting in her own spoiled way and it was weird getting in her head. Because of Leah's home life and a family secret, she has sought out love in all the wrong ways and definitely wrong place. She really just wants to be loved and cherished but instead of accepting Caleb and how he truly felt, she's become obsessed with him. In the first book, I thought she was the master manipulator but after reading this book, it's clear that she is just so used to getting things her way and taking what she wants. I'm glad that she gets a bit of a wakeup call. <br /><br />Some of the events were almost too unbelievable...such as dropping Estella off at some unknown daycare and then drinking and driving. I think it was good that Leah was forced to take care of Estella by herself. <br /><br />Caleb, Caleb, Caleb...I still like him and I was glad to get some answers about why he did things as well. There are still some things that are unclear and I. Can. Not. Wait. for his book. I liked how he bonded with Estella and that he finally stood up to Leah then and later. And Cherry Garcia...that killed me. <br /><br />Olivia how I missed her!! She just wasn't in this story enough...even though she was talked about, she was only in a few actual scenes. I was surprised that things went forward with her and Noah and I'm not sure how that will be handled in the future. The birthday present was very interesting and I'm hoping we get more about that too. <br /><br />If you liked the first book, I would recommend reading this one. You really don't want to miss out on anything before Caleb's book. <br /><br />The plot thickens....yes, unfortunately I still have questions and they are spoilers:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />1. Who's your daddy? So the obvious choice is that it's Seth's and while I'm not ruling him out, I can't but wonder about Seth's and Caleb's Dad...a known womanizer. <br /><br />2. Guilty or not? I was surprised we didn't get more information about the rapist. The rumor is that Seth (a police sergeant) is pinning this on Dobson...the problem is that I can't understand why unless it's just so Seth can have everything that Caleb has had? <br /><br />3. Sam the Manny...I really like him but could he really be with Leah? it does seem possible. <br /><br />4. Noah...how could Olivia ever hurt him? But...we now know that Caleb does know him and it is possible that he hired Noah to watch Olivia. If something like that is true, that could lead to a fallout but I still would hate for Olivia to get hurt again. <br /><br />5. Family ties...Court and her suicide attempt, Leah and her suicide attempt....Cash?? How will that all work out?<br /><br />6. Cheater or not?? I still want answers to what "technically" didn't happened with Caleb and that woman in his office and why!!<br /><br />7. Home Sweet Home....I still need the deets on that one!<br /><br /><br />Here's some questions I had from the first book and thought I would address them and see if there were any answers:<br /><br />1. The ring in the sock drawer....I was hoping he had bought that for Olivia and IDK it just seems like it has more significance. <i>Yes!! he did buy it for her!</i><br /><br />2. The Rapists ~ Dobson Scott Orchard aka Devon.....there has to be more to the story and I'm wondering who he is. Could he be a half brother to Olivia? <i>Well now we know he has been arrested and Olivia is defending him but we don't know why!</i><br /><br />3. Where is Caleb's brother all this time....I'm even questioning if he is the rapist. <i>Still think he is involved</i><br /><br />4. If Leah does get pregnant, all bets are that its Turners!! <br />Remember "the seventeen curious stains on my ivory sofa and the twelve shoe scuffs on my wall"?? hmmmmm. And who was the girl Caleb cheated with? I don't put that past Leah either! <i>Well, at this point it's still a mystery but I'm leaning towards Seth or his and Caleb's Dad.</i> <br /><br />5. What was the deal with Caleb not pushing for sex with Olivia? He was really upset when he found her in the hotel room and the condom wrapper. Did he want her as a virgin? Seems like there is something about that too. <i>Hopefully this will be answered in Caleb's book.</i><br /><br />6. WHAT THE HECK HAPPENED IN ROME???? everything seem to be headed a certain way and then bammm....it did a 180?? now 3 years later, she's getting married to Noah??? and what was up w/her thinking she saw Caleb instead? <i>Still don't know but I. Am. Shocked. She married Noah!</i><br /><br />7. Speaking of Noah, I just can't see them getting married. Noah saw straight through things, right to the heart of the matter. Could he live with knowing that Olivia would always love Caleb? <i>I guess he can but there's obviously more to the story.</i><br /><br />8. what if the epilogue is NOT real??? <i>Dang...it was real!</i><br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Favorite quotes:<br /><br />♦ “You said you would never hurt me.” <br /><br />His eyes are frigid. “That was before you fucked with my daughter.”<br /><br />♥ “You never quite stop loving someone when you're in that deep.”<br /><br />♦ “I’ve been someone different with you. Someone I don’t understand.”<br /><br />♦ “You remind me of a cheap reality show, Leah. You’re shallow, and you pretend to be stupid for God only knows what reason.”<br /><br />♥ “I didn’t choose her,” his voice breaks. “Love is illogical. You fall into it like a manhole. Then you’re just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love.”<br /><br />eta: I can't stop listening to this...<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1MwjX4dG72s">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1MwjX4...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11857378574673257698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_424874890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/424874890" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/424874890?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer424874890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13724971372893486224"><b>My name is Leah and I will do anything to keep my husband.</b> <br/><br/>How could I absolutely <b>LOVE</b> a book about a character i despise? Because Tarryn Fisher is brilliant. Love her writing! The Opportunist was one of the first books I ever read that didn’t give me a HEA and I didn’t care- It was just that good. This book, I didn’t want a HEA- not for Leah anyway. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>Whoever she was, I would wipe her from his memory in no time at all. Why? Because I was the best of the best: the Godiva, the Maserati, the perf</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText13724971372893486224" style="display:none"><b>My name is Leah and I will do anything to keep my husband.</b> <br /><br />How could I absolutely <b>LOVE</b> a book about a character i despise? Because Tarryn Fisher is brilliant. Love her writing! The Opportunist was one of the first books I ever read that didn’t give me a HEA and I didn’t care- It was just that good. This book, I didn’t want a HEA- not for Leah anyway. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Whoever she was, I would wipe her from his memory in no time at all. Why? Because I was the best of the best: the Godiva, the Maserati, the perfect colorless diamond. I could improve anyone’s life- especially this man’s.</i>
</b><br /><br />Think of all those women you know, the really terrible ones... all of those bad name you like to call them- Leah is all of that and more. By far one of the least likable characters ever. She is a mess. She is selfish, manipulative, bitchy, and just awful. I thought maybe she would have some redeemable qualities- nope. This is a woman, who after giving birth, her first thought about her new born baby daughter is: <i> I am going to have to share my husband with another woman... again.</i> Yup. I still hate her. But now I feel like I understand her. <br /><br />Leah is evil, but she is also funny. It was nice to see what was going on in that crazy head of hers. I loved the interactions between her and her ‘manny’ Sam-<br /><i>
  <b>“How do I get him to come home?” <br />“Get a new personality and learn to shut the fuck up.”<br /><br />“Shit, I forgot. It’s hard to remember that a cold shrew like you is actually a mother.”<br /><br />“Wow. You grew a heart, and all it took was seven boxes of chocolate covered raisins.”<br /><br />  “You are the single most offensive women I have ever met, you know that?”</b>
</i><br /><br />I really liked Sam. Even though I didn’t get as much of Olivia as I liked, I was happy to get more of Cammie! <br /><br />The further along in the book you got, things started to unravel. I feel like a lot of my questions got answered, but there is still a lot I need to know<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like- Is Estella Seth’s baby? And what the hell was in Olivia’s birthday box from Caleb? And what is up with Leah’s sister? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>! Hoping that in the third book, everything will come to light. As everything started happening- especially the last 30% of the book, I found myself quoting Leah... <i>Sons of guns and motherfuckers.</i> There were some definite bombs dropped at the end of this one... Not sure if I was happy with the ending or not, but the series is not over yet! Please tell me the third book will be out sooner rather than later... I have a feeling it will be the best one yet! And it’s from Caleb’s pov(and I love Caleb!) Although I am a bit confllicted on what I want to happen...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I WANT CALEB &amp; OLIVIA TOGETHER! But it just feels wrong... as much as I love Caleb, I also love Noah.. hmmm  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Some of my favorite quotes that make me even more excited for book 3 <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“You never quite stop loving someone when you’re in that deep.”<br /><br />That was the worst possible thing about love; no matter how hard you tried, you could never forget the person who had your heart. <br /><br />“I didn’t choose her. Love is illogical. You fall into it like a man-hole. Then you’re just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love.”</b>
</i><br /><br />If you haven’t read this series- you are really missing out!!!!!</span>

<div id="review_478329092" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478329092" />
    <a title="Brenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna"><img alt="Brenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580475762p2/12928663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478329092?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenna" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna">Brenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478329092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7533812861571376686"><b>
  <i>"Sons of guns and motherfuckers."</i>
</b><br/><br/>After reading <i>The Opportunist</i> for the first time a few days ago, I was <b>beyond</b> excited to start <i>Dirty Red</i>. I just couldn't imagine reading a book about someone I <b>DO NOT</b> want the hero of this series to be with. Even though I never wanted Leah & Caleb together, I went in with an open mind. I didn't have immediate hatred for Leah after <i>The Opportunist</i> like many did. I never actually <b>liked</b> Leah, but I didn't <b>hate</b> her either. <br/><br/>Yeah, well... that all changed after th</span>
  <span id="freeText7533812861571376686" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Sons of guns and motherfuckers."</i>
</b><br /><br />After reading <i>The Opportunist</i> for the first time a few days ago, I was <b>beyond</b> excited to start <i>Dirty Red</i>. I just couldn't imagine reading a book about someone I <b>DO NOT</b> want the hero of this series to be with. Even though I never wanted Leah &amp; Caleb together, I went in with an open mind. I didn't have immediate hatred for Leah after <i>The Opportunist</i> like many did. I never actually <b>liked</b> Leah, but I didn't <b>hate</b> her either. <br /><br />Yeah, well... that all changed after the <b>FIRST</b> freaking page of <i>Dirty Red</i>. Leah is officially on my shit list. I couldn't get over how completely self centered she is. We all know Olivia has done her fair share of shitty things and made bad decisions, but she at least has redeemable qualities and I just <b>like</b> her, plain and simple. I cannot say the same about Leah. My general feelings about a character are usually based on whether or not I would actually like the person in real life. I would NOT like Leah in my life, she is not someone I would want to be around at all! <br /><br /><i>"I have done a number of things to keep this man. I have lied and cheated. I have been sexy and meek, fierce and vulnerable. I have been everything but myself."</i><br /><br />I honestly believe the way Leah behaves in <i>Dirty Red</i> <b>IS</b> Leah being herself. I don't understand how it couldn't be? Even though she tries to put on a show for Caleb, her true colors inevitably come out. She just can't help herself. We do get some insight into her past and perhaps some reasons about why she is the way she is. I just never felt like those were excuses for her fucked up personality. Eventually I just had to laugh at the things Leah would think because they were just so <b>wrong</b>. Even though she drove me a little crazy, she was still entertaining and I loved hating her the entire time, so kudos to Tarryn for pulling that off! Big time!<br /><br />I really missed Olivia in this one though. After being in her head for <i>The Opportunist</i>, it was a very weird transition to go from all to practically nothing. I also wish there was more Caleb! Even though his moments weren't as frequent as I would have liked, he completely stole my heart! Him with Estella is just about the sweetest thing ever! See that there &gt;&gt;&gt; yup, that's my heart melted in a puddle... :) <br /><br />My favorite addition to this crazy f-ed up story was SAM! He is so honest with Leah and says whatever he thinks in that moment. I love him! Oh man... there are just too many quotable moments, but here are a few of my favorites:<br /><br /><i>“Why would he marry a girl like you?” <br /><br />“Shit, I forgot,” he says. “It’s hard to remember that a cold shrew like you is actually a mother.” <br /><br />“You were a selfish, self-centered bitch... God, I can’t believe I work for you. I feel sick.” </i><br /><br />As much as I wish I could tell you that this book brought answers to questions from <i>The Opportunist</i> and wrapped it all up in a pretty little bow, I can't. It seriously fucked my head up even worse and I feel like I need to read both books again at least <i>a few</i> more times! Which I'm sure I will do, without a doubt. So obviously I <b>LOVED</b> it even though I <b>HATED</b> it. Just read it, but beware that you will be seriously obsessed for god knows how long... Enjoy! :)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7533812861571376686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508469690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6432520234957083589"><b>My name is Leah, and I will do anything to keep my husband.</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453076218i/17778660.gif' alt=' photo bitch crazy pll_zpsvzfmbgwf.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>You think Olivia is manipulative? Meet dirty red. I thought I might feel bad for her while reading this, but that couldn't be anywhere farther from what I felt towards her. She is awful. She acts like a good person, but she is really thinking anything but nice thoughts. She is the most selfish person ever. She sees Caleb as her prize. She wants the idea of a man like Caleb, but has no idea what love is supposed to be like.<br/><br/><b>I have done a n</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6432520234957083589" style="display:none"><b>My name is Leah, and I will do anything to keep my husband.</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453076218i/17778660.gif" alt=" photo bitch crazy pll_zpsvzfmbgwf.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You think Olivia is manipulative? Meet dirty red. I thought I might feel bad for her while reading this, but that couldn't be anywhere farther from what I felt towards her. She is awful. She acts like a good person, but she is really thinking anything but nice thoughts. She is the most selfish person ever. She sees Caleb as her prize. She wants the idea of a man like Caleb, but has no idea what love is supposed to be like.<br><br><b>I have done a number of things to keep this man. I have lied and cheated. I have been sexy and meek, fierce and vulnerable. I have been everything but myself.</b><br><br>She made me so mad because of Estella. She can't stand being around her own baby. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ What kind of person leaves their 2 week old baby at daycare and forgets about her for HOURS?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Caleb had stars in his eyes for her since she was born. At least little Estella has Caleb.<br><br>As we see in The Opportunist, Caleb isn't as innocent as he seems. It seems like he is trying to do the right thing, but most of the time is just making the complete wrong decision. I wanted to smack him a time or two. We really don't get much of Olivia in this, which made me pretty sad. Olivia has grown on me since the beginning of The Opportunist. She seems to make the wrong decisions most of the time, but she's not the only one.<br><br>I really enjoyed the character of Sam, the Manny for Estella. He was so blunt with Leah all the time. He saw her for what she was, a selfish bitch, but I think he kind of respected that she didn't try to hide her bitchiness from him. He didn't try to play nice with her and it seemed in the end they had a genuine friendship. Their dialogues were so funny. That was one redeeming thing I saw about Leah. I loved the scenes with her and Sam.<br><br><b>Leah: 'How do I get him to come home?'<br>Sam: 'Get a new personality and learn to shut the fuck up.'</b><br><br>Again, in Dirty Red the story line jumps from present to past. This is something I really liked in The Opportunist and it also worked well for this book. We go back in time to see how Caleb and Leah met and other different scenes covering a lot of time within The Opportunist. I liked seeing what Leah felt and what was really happening in her and Caleb's relationship during the "amnesia" spell.<br><br>After that bomb was dropped on us at the very end, my mouth dropped open! I didn't see that coming. I don't know whether to believe it or not!<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_403256370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog"><img alt=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486609762p2/2607684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/403256370?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" href="/user/show/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog"> Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer403256370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17590827260631958813"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389471i/750567._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>See more reviews like this at <a href='http://readingbookslikeaboss.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'> Reading Books Like a Boss</a></b><br/><br/><b>*DO NOT READ MY REVIEW IF YOU HAVE NOT READ THE OPPORTUNIST. IT MAY CONTAIN SPOILERS.<br/><br/>I'M WARNING YOU...<br/><br/><i>"My name is Leah, and I will do anything to keep my husband."</i></b><br/><br/>I was extremely scared and apprehensive about reading this book. I hated HATED Leah in The Opportunist. Even though she made only brief appearances in book #1, she left quite the impression and a horrible taste in my mouth. Those feelings only intensified when I read Dirty Red. I</span>
  <span id="freeText17590827260631958813" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389471i/750567._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>See more reviews like this at <a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener"> Reading Books Like a Boss</a></b><br><br><b>*DO NOT READ MY REVIEW IF YOU HAVE NOT READ THE OPPORTUNIST. IT MAY CONTAIN SPOILERS.<br><br>I'M WARNING YOU...<br><br><i>"My name is Leah, and I will do anything to keep my husband."</i></b><br><br>I was extremely scared and apprehensive about reading this book. I hated HATED Leah in The Opportunist. Even though she made only brief appearances in book #1, she left quite the impression and a horrible taste in my mouth. Those feelings only intensified when I read Dirty Red. It's been more than a week since I read the book, and I'm still reeling and analyzing what the crap happened.<br><br>Leah was another player in the Caleb and Olivia's lying game. I would argue she outplayed both Caleb and Olivia in this book. From the very first page, I was enraged and wanted to slap her. Why in the world did Caleb marry this monster? Her self-centeredness knows no bounds. She always thinks of herself. She is obsessed with Olivia even though Caleb and Olivia presumably don't speak.<br><blockquote>"What power does she have over him? I want to run at him, pound my fists against his chest for always mentally comparing me to her. Or am I the only mentally comparing myself to her? God, life is so messed up."<br><br>"Caleb is looking at me, but he is not seeing me. I want to throw up. How fragile is my marriage, if all he has to do is look at her and I cease to exist?"</blockquote><br>Leah's dreadful character was somewhat redeemed (I still hate her with a passion). She grew up in a loveless household where her mother and father doted on her sister, Courtney, and treated Leah like she was a piece of trash. Courtney was popular in school, while Leah was an outcast. The tables turned after Leah took up for her sister after Courtney's best friend stabbed her in the back. Thus, manipulative, lying, self-absorbed Leah was born.<br><blockquote>"I liked how easily I could make boys follow me around by dangling sex in their faces. I liked the way their girlfriends came to school with puffy red eyes from crying, after they found out their boyfriends had cheated on them."</blockquote><br>I missed Olivia A LOT while reading Dirty Red. I missed her inner dialogue and her vodka-infused baths. I missed Olivia's Caleb. I missed them being together. Even though they were mostly absent from the present, the reader got glimpses into their story through Leah's POV. There were some pretty shocking revelations that had me gasping, awwwhing, and rooting for "Colivia."<br><blockquote>"I didn't choose her," his voice breaks. "Love is illogical. You fall into it like a manhole. Then you're just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love."</blockquote><br>I have Great Expectations for "Thief," Book #3. Finally, we'll get to hear Caleb's side of the story, and hopeful, Caleb and Olivia will have their happy ever after. If they don't get their HEA, I will 1.) die, 2.) write own ending and 3.) shun Tarryn Fisher for all of eternity.<br><br>Tarryn Fisher is an absolute genius. She is the master of ambiguity. The reader doesn't really know who knows what at what point in time. Now if you'll excuse me, I need to go make a timeline.<br><br>_________________________<br><br><strong>Find more of my reviews and other bookish things here:</strong><br><br><strong>✥ My blog <a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">R</a><a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">eading Books Like a Boss</a></strong><br><strong> ✥ Like on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/ReadingBooksLikeABoss" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></strong><br><strong> ✥ Follow on <a href="http://twitter.com/ireadlikeaboss" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></strong></span>

<div id="review_686942074" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686942074" />
    <a title="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog"><img alt="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429608146p2/12994342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/686942074?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" href="/user/show/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog">Smitten&#39;s Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=angst-filled-reads">angst-filled-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=like-marmite">like-marmite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=rich-guy-hero">rich-guy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=head-fuck">head-fuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer686942074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17604399406453956887"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867066._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391840i/754514._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok, this might be a little disjointed, because I'm already half way through <i>Thief</i>. I hardly ever start another book before I've written a review for the previous one, but I just couldn't help myself. <br/><br/>I raced through <i>Dirty Red</i> yesterday, finished it at about midnight and then dived straight into <i>Thief</i>. I can confirm, I <i>definitely</i> made the right decision in waiting until the third book was released. How on earth some of you guys sat tight at the end of <i>Dirty Red</i> and waited for long for Caleb's boo</span>
  <span id="freeText17604399406453956887" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867066._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391840i/754514._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, this might be a little disjointed, because I'm already half way through <i>Thief</i>. I hardly ever start another book before I've written a review for the previous one, but I just couldn't help myself. <br><br>I raced through <i>Dirty Red</i> yesterday, finished it at about midnight and then dived straight into <i>Thief</i>. I can confirm, I <i>definitely</i> made the right decision in waiting until the third book was released. How on earth some of you guys sat tight at the end of <i>Dirty Red</i> and waited for long for Caleb's book, I will neeeever know! Oh my goodness, talk about dropping a bomb! Ok, we'll go there in a minute. First things first.<br><br>So, this is Leah's book. I absolutely could not understand <i>why</i> on God's green earth, we were getting an entire book from the villain's POV. I felt like having a full on, foot stamping, snot flinging, fist thumping tantrum, knowing I had to get through it, before I got to what I hoped would be the good bit.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>My name is Leah, and I will do anything to keep my husband.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867067._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't really know how to fill this review. How many ways are there to express your hatred for a character??<br>I don't like Leah.<br>I strongly dislike Leah.<br>I hate Leah.<br>I wish Leah would be run over by a bus.<br>I wish Leah would die in a tragic boating accident.<br>I wish Leah would spontaneously combust and cease to exist.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867068.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You get the idea. I'm reeeally not a fan! <b>Team Cal-ivia</b> all the way!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867069._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"They spark. When they're together, it's like putting a hurricane and a tornado in the same room - you can feel the tension. I didn't believe in the cliche of soul mates until I saw them together."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>But this book was definitely a necessary evil. I really can't say too much without giving things away. Just know that from the first sentence, Tarryn Fisher will knock your socks off, and then she'll just keep on knocking until the very last word of the book!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I have lied and cheated. I have been sexy and meek, fierce and vulnerable. I have been everything but myself.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867070.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book continues, as the previous one did, to go back and forth through time. Past and present. And there is so much going on in this book that it just adds to the mind blow. You get to see Caleb and Leah's relationship through her eyes. You get a lot more insight into why Caleb made the decisions he made in book one. How things came about. Why things weren't straight forward, etc. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"How do I get him to come home?"<br>"Get a new personality and learn to shut the fuck up."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I felt like I was on drugs, reading this book... my head was buzzing and my eyes were wide. I had emotional whiplash, a racing heart and sweaty palms. It's all a bit of a blur. I spent the entire time wanting to knock Leah out and feeling guilty about being so mean about Caleb.<br><br>On that point. Caleb does redeem himself. Literally, within the first couple of pages, I felt bad for judging Caleb so harshly in book one. I was <i>so</i> angry with him, and now I feel bad.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I didn't choose her," his voice breaks. "Love is illogical. You fall into it like a manhole. Then you're just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>There is barely <i>any</i> Olivia in this book. Yet, still, the love Caleb feels for her is palpable. I love it. It's delicious. And it smacks Leah right between the eyes. Ha! But it rips Caleb apart. It's painful to see. He's a good man and he's trying to do the right thing. The man needs a cuddle. And, I'm a great cuddler. Just saying.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Scars should stay where fate put them.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>One thing I do want to say in this review, because I got so carried away with the storyline in the first book and didn't give this enough page space... Tarryn Fisher deserves some kind of award. The woman is freakin' Ah.Ma.Zing!!!! Honestly, she is supremely gifted. You completely forget you are even reading a book at all. The character development is second to none. I feel like I know these characters. Like, they can't possibly <i>not</i> be real. There is so much to each and every one of them, I feel like I could predict their reactions to things, I feel like I could drop them a text when things are going bad for them. Obviously, not Leah. I wouldn't drop her a text. Dog shit through her letter box, maybe. Or a bomb, perhaps. But not a text. Anyway, I digress. Tarryn Fisher is a natural born writer. It's what she was put on this earth to do. Despite the fact that she has caused me so much pain, suffering, sleep deprivation and heartache, I'm totally girl-crushing on the lady!<br><br>So, back to <i>Dirty Red</i>. Leah is that. Dirty. Foul. Defiled. Nasty. Contaminated. Sullied. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867071._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I was about ten on the poison scale. If he needed venom, I could inject directly into his neck.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867072.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She fights filthy. She's screwed up. Totally. She is rotten to the core. <i>But</i>, and gah, I hate to say this, I did feel a small glimmer of empathy for her. She has been through a torrid time. She has nobody. <i>Nobody</i>. Okay, so most of it has been brought upon by her own wickedness, but she doesn't really know any different. She has never had a good role model, she's never been loved and she has never been respected. As a consequence, she has no idea how to be a decent human being, she doesn't understand true love and she doesn't have an ounce of self respect. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I knew he never loved me like he loved her, but I wanted him anyway. I knew his love for me was conditional, but I wanted him anyway. I knew I was second choice, but I wanted him anyway.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I do believe that she thinks she loves Caleb, in her own twisted way. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"A woman shouldn't have to fight that hard to be with a man. He should just want her..."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>But, still. See previous notes... I do hate the bitch. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867073.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And if I hadn't hated her throughout the book already, the ending, God, if that didn't seal her fate. Wow, the hag knows no bounds. Give me a break! She needs to work out when enough is enough.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867074._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I completely didn't see the ending coming. I didn't know whether to laugh or scream! And I didn't miss a single beat before I started Thief. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Their story will never be over."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>So, I'm feeling weird about giving this five stars and <i>The Opportunist</i> four, because I hated Leah, and this is her book. And because I enjoyed most of book #1 more than I enjoyed this book. But I can see more, now, where the story is going. I feel like I'm on the home stretch now and I'm feeling hopeful. The series is coming together and I'm excited, nervous, apprehensive... I just don't feel that, as a series, I can keep giving it four stars. I'm so in love with these characters and their story, now. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You never quite stop loving someone when you're in that deep."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431937i/867075.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, the fifth star is more for the series as a whole, as it is, so far. Because Leah gets a big fat zero stars and a slap round the mouth. But, the jury is still out. If this doesn't end how I want it to end, I will not be held accountable for my actions. You have be warned.<br><br>P.S. I don't have the head-space for a collage right now. Sorry.<br><br><b><i>Dirty Red</i> Statistics</b><br><b>Steam Rating (out of 5):</b> ♥<br><b>Ending:</b> Cliffhanger<br><b>Series:</b> ✓ (<i>Love Me With Lies</i> series)<br><b>Reading Order:</b><br>Book #1 - <i>The Opportunist</i><br>Book #2 - <i>Dirty Red</i><br>Book #3 - <i>Thief</i><br><b>Can this be read as a standalone?</b> No<br><b>Themes:</b><br>Lies<br>Love Triangle<br><b>Warning. This book includes... </b><br>Love triangle<br>Cheating<br>Lies<br><b>Writing:</b> Fantastic<br><br>UK AMAZON: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/Dirty-Love-With-Lies-ebook/dp/B00ARNWQ98/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1375870698&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=dirty+red">http://www.amazon.co.uk/Dirty-Love-Wi...</a><br>US AMAZON: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/Dirty-Love-With-Lies-ebook/dp/B00ARNWQ98/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1375870698&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=dirty+red">http://www.amazon.com/Dirty-Love-With...</a><br><br><b>

<div id="review_673517957" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/673517957" />
    <a title="Catarina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11538033-catarina"><img alt="Catarina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514808293p2/11538033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/673517957?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catarina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catarina" href="/user/show/11538033-catarina">Catarina</a>
      </span>

        rated it

  <span id="freeText9659661705278030336" style="display:none"> <b> 4 psychotic and bitchy stars! </b><br><br>I don't think I've ever read a book as fast as I’ve read this one. I was postponing the reading of this book so I could read it closer to Thief’s releasing date. The awesome mindfuck was all here again. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380430022ra/861948.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is told under Leah’s POV and we get to know how she and Caleb ended up together (I really love this past flashbacks) and everything that happened after the end of the first one and after she had he baby. <br>And after reading her story, believe me, I still hate her like crazy, but it’s definitely not easy knowing that you’ll always be a second choice. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430022i/861949.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’ve got to say that this was the first time I liked so much a book where I actually hate the female heroine. <br>Leah is a bitch, is very aware of that and has no intentions of changing. We see that Caleb is also not so innocent in the middle of all this, but we can’t stop loving him anyway. <br><br>This is not as angst as the previous one (Thank god!!) but it still makes you bleed a little. This author is a genius and her writing and ability to create completely awesome and a psychotic stories grab us from the very first page. <br>And that end… god, that end! I need the third one, now! </span>

  <span id="freeText15707587389628787779" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400128i/775030._SX540_.jpg" width="125" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>♥♥♥ 4 CRAZY BITCH STARS ♥♥♥</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794785i/596848._SX540_.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430049i/862037._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"I have done a number of things to keep this man. I have lied and cheated. I have been sexy and meek, fierce and vulnerable. I have been everything but myself. He is mine right now, but I am never enough for him (...) I don't know what he's looking for. I wish I did… <br><br>I am who I am. <br><br>My name is Leah, and I will do anything to keep my husband."<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Well, I had no idea what to expect when reading this book. I was actually very close to <b>not</b> reading it because I didn't like her in the first book. But then I finally did. Within the first few pages... I <b>HATED</b> Leah. She was <b>heartless, selfish, manipulative, crazy </b> and the <b>Queen of all bitches</b>, I tell ya!! I had never been inside the mind of character like her. She was full of <b>insecurities</b>. She liked to <b>judge</b> everyone else, but all I kept thinking was she should look in the mirror. She disliked it when people looked at her with any look other than <b>admiration, lust,</b> and <b>envy</b>. She wanted to be centre of attention.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445452995ra/16652313.gif" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"Caleb is a pretty nice guy"<br>"Yes? And?"<br>"Why would he marry a girl like you?"<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>That was exactly what I wanted to do at the beginning of this book. How could she so <b>cold-hearted</b>?? I wanted to beat the crap out of her. I seriously don't know <b>how</b> Caleb could have stayed with her as long as he did. The story, just like in the first one, alternates from presesnt to past. You get an <b>insight</b> of Leah's upbringing and how her relationship with Caleb started. I will admit, as much as I hated this <b>psycho</b> woman, I did feel for her because of the way she was raised. She is pretty much <b>seeking</b> what she has <b>never</b> had, <b>love</b>, but going about it all wrong. Still, it <b>doesn't</b> excuse her for her behaviour. She could have changed her ways, but instead she <b>chose</b> to be a spoiled snob just like the family that raised her.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>“Love is illogical. You fall into it like a manhole. Then you're just stuck. You die in love more than you live in love.”<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445452995ra/16652314.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Leah is struggling to <b>keep</b> Caleb in her life. He is slowly distancing himself from her, but she <b>won't</b> give him up without a fight. I kinda feel bad for Leah because I don't know if she will ever be happy. But then again, she brought it all on to herself. She <b>tried</b> to be honest in hopes of making Caleb stay by revealing what she has done. All she ends up doing is <b>hurting</b> Caleb, and making him angry.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>He thought Olivia could hurt him, I'll hurt him worse. I'll keep hurting him.<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445452995ra/16652315.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That <b>ending</b>... how can I not continue the next book <b>right</b> away!?! I must read it book <b>now</b>! I need to know how it's all going to play out. How could Leah still choose to be a freaking bitch!? I just <b>really</b> want Caleb to find <b>happiness</b>. I'm not sure if the bitch <b>Olivia</b> can give it to him, just like I know the bitch <b>Leah</b> can't. But who knows... What is up with <b>Caleb</b> and mean bitches anyway?? Well.. now I'm off to read the next!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"Some people never change. I guess I'm one of them."<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794785i/596848._SX540_.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15707587389628787779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_594983975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/594983975" />
    <a title="☆ Sammy ☆彡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14144676-sammy"><img alt="☆ Sammy ☆彡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462053159p2/14144676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/594983975?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☆ Sammy ☆彡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☆ Sammy ☆彡" href="/user/show/14144676-sammy">☆ Sammy ☆彡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14144676-sammy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14144676-sammy?shelf=emotionally-intense">emotionally-intense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14144676-sammy?shelf=signed-books">signed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer594983975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4575604091614152887">To be completely honest, I was not looking forward to an entire book in Leah's POV. I didn't like her character in The Opportunist and I really didn't want to read about her relationship/marriage with Caleb because he belongs with Olivia! That being said, this book had me completely hooked and I couldn't put it down.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418305ra/828177.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Dirty Red continues from where the Opportunist left off. You learn a lot about Leah's past and events that made her into the person that she is. You also get a glimpse into Leah and </span>
  <span id="freeText4575604091614152887" style="display:none">To be completely honest, I was not looking forward to an entire book in Leah's POV. I didn't like her character in The Opportunist and I really didn't want to read about her relationship/marriage with Caleb because he belongs with Olivia! That being said, this book had me completely hooked and I couldn't put it down.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418305ra/828177.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dirty Red continues from where the Opportunist left off. You learn a lot about Leah's past and events that made her into the person that she is. You also get a glimpse into Leah and Caleb's relationship.. from their initial meeting, through dating and getting married, and finally you see what happens in their marriage after the events of the Opportunist. Like The Opportunist, the chapters bounce back and forth between the past and present. <br><br>I still <b>HATE</b> Leah.. a lot. In this book you see just how deceitful, manipulative, and hateful she really is. Even though this book helped me to understand her better, I can honestly say the understanding didn't make me like her or feel sorry for her for that matter. Having difficult circumstances in life doesn't mean she has to be a terrible person because of them.<br><br><b>To Dirty Red:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399068ra/771898.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Caleb was absolutely amazing though :) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I love how he didn't fall for Leah's shit and he is such an awesome father to Estella regardless of whether or not he is the biological father <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Another one of my favorite parts of the story was the manny Sam! I loved how he was very honest and blunt with Leah. <br><br><b>"Caleb is a pretty nice guy"<br>"Yes? And?"<br>"Why would he marry a girl like you?"</b><br><br>The last chapter of this book was crazy! There were a lot of truths revealed that totally changed everything! Since I am now officially obssessed with this series.. 4 solid stars!<br><br><b>Memorable quotes:</b><br><br>Cammie to Leah: "When they're together, it's like putting a hurricane and a tornado in the same room - you can feel the tension. I didn't believe in the cliche of soul mates until I saw them together." Cammie's description is absolutely perfect!<br><br>Leah: "I thought you loved your husband." Olivia: "I love yours too." This scene put the biggest smile on my face. It was nice to see Olivia shove that little tidbit in Leah's face. I felt like it knocked Leah off her self appointed pedestal for a minute.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4575604091614152887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iBeKmyjKjS3xrepORnLmsaSMRh6O+RQ1rls9u0BdFACyMeNJk5RERVaGXi+xh+xuctOh1kB0mlL1JXsKjR7mmg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Agmg8mGdRN7p4d32t+d+HEZzj9jt9TBlcqRpO9NQnbY4L8kg2sONtk7KaZdAEnTDkCxoECN4vgIp2i+KHhNvLA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13867781187249116323">I would like to write a novel that every, single person loves, but not even J.K. Rowling could do that. Instead, I try to write stories that pull on people's emotions. I believe that sadness is the most powerful emotion, and swirled with regret the two become a dominating force. I love villains. Three of my favorites are Mother Gothel, Gaston and the Evil Queen who all suffered from a pretty wicke</span>
  <span id="freeText13867781187249116323" style="display:none">I would like to write a novel that every, single person loves, but not even J.K. Rowling could do that. Instead, I try to write stories that pull on people's emotions. I believe that sadness is the most powerful emotion, and swirled with regret the two become a dominating force. I love villains. Three of my favorites are Mother Gothel, Gaston and the Evil Queen who all suffered from a pretty wicked case of vanity (like me). I like to make these personality types the center of my stories. <br />I love rain, Coke, Starbucks and sarcasm. I hate bad adjectives and the word "smolder". If you read my book-I love you. If you hate my book-I still love you, but please don't be mean to me; I'm half badass, half cry baby. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13867781187249116323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
